<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lie">Lie<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lie" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lie means the relation of the foetus to the long axis of the uterus. It may be longitudinal, oblique or transverse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="presentation">Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The presenting part of the foetus is that part which is in or over the pelvic brim. Its position is examined in relation to the cervix. It could be vertex, face, or a breech. However, 95% of all presentations are cephalic, and the presenting part is usually the vertex.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="position">Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The position describes the relationship of a selected part of the foetus to the maternal pelvis. For example, in a vertex presentation the selected part is the occiput. With face presentation it is the chin, and with a breech presentation, it is the sacrum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="attitude">Attitude<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attitude" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>he pelvis is a curved passage with different diameters at the inlet, mid-cavity and outlet as you saw in unit two. The foetus, therefore, has to adapt itself to the shape, size, and curve of the pelvis at different levels as it descends.</p>
<p>To be able to manage labour skilfully, you need to understand the natural movements made by the baby so that, when assisting in delivery, you can follow the movements rather than oppose them.</p>
<p>The factors, which influence the mechanism of labour, are known as the three 'Ps': power, passage, and passenger.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="power">Power<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#power" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The stronger the contraction in a well prepared mother, the better the outcome of labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="passage">Passage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#passage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The size, shape and resistance of the birth canal including the bony pelvis, cervix, vagina and pelvic floor may speed up or slow down the process of delivery. A gynaecoid pelvis and a fully dilated cervix speed up the process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="passenger">Passenger<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#passenger" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This refers to the size, lie and presentation of the foetus, as well as the placenta and membranes. For the foetus, a vertex presentation makes labour shorter as the presenting part fits well on the cervical Os and stimulates the cervix to dilate faster.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 106 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>It is important to remember that descent occurs throughout and as mentioned earlier, ninety five per cent of all presentations are cephalic, and the presenting part is usually the vertex. This areas boundaries include the bregma or the anterior fontanel, the perietal eminences and the posterior fontanel. The presenting diameter is, therefore, the smallest - 9.5cm. In order to present with the smallest diameter, the head must be well flexed on the neck with the chin touching the chest. As the leading part meets resistance of the pelvic floor it rotates 1/8th forwards until it comes under the symphysis pubis.</p>
<p>The mechanism of labour in a cephalic vertex presentation includes the following steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Engagement and descent</li>
<li>Internal rotation</li>
<li>Birth by extension of the head</li>
<li>Restitution and external rotation</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at each of these steps in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="engagement-and-descent">Engagement and Descent<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#engagement-and-descent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Engagement is the descent of the presenting diameter through the pelvic brim. The head usually engages late in pregnancy in the primigravida while in the multipara it does not engage till labour starts. The head enters the pelvic brim in oblique diameter with sub occipital frontal diameter (10.5cm). With good uterine contraction, there is more flexion of the head. The head engages with sub occipital bregmatic (9.5 cms) oblique diameter of the pelvis brim.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-rotation">Internal Rotation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The head rotates 1/8th of a circle. Such a rotation is achieved by the action of the uterine muscle pushing downwards. The pointed vertex presents on the broad levator ani muscle. When the vertex reaches the perineum, the occiput turns from the posterior to the anterior position. Anteriorly there is more room for further descent. When the occiput is below the symphysis pubis, crowning takes place.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-rotation-of-the-foetus">Internal rotation of the foetus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-foetus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-9e34dc1c.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="birth-by-extension-of-the-head">Birth By Extension of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#birth-by-extension-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the occiput has escaped from under the symphysis pubis, the head extends forward. The nape of the neck is pressed firmly against the pubic arch. This extension of the head causes the anterior part to stretch the perineum gradually. Further extension allows the sinciput, face and chin to escape the perineum and the head is born by extension. Extension is the result of action from two forces. The abdominal and thoracic muscles exert downward pressure. The pelvic floor and perineum resist this pressure and push the head forward and upward through the weak area, which is the vagina.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sinciput-and-face-delivered">Sinciput and face delivered<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sinciput-and-face-delivered" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-164cd310.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="restitution">Restitution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restitution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The head turns 1/8 of the circle to the left, back to where it was before. This rotation takes place to undo the twist, which occurred during the</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>previous internal rotation. This 'undoing of the twist' is known as restitution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-rotation-of-the-shoulder">Internal Rotation of the shoulder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-shoulder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the head is passing through the level of the ischial spines and the outlet in anterior posterior position, the shoulders enter in the oblique diameter of the pelvis and rotate forward 1/8 of a circle. The shoulders are now in the anterior posterior diameter of the outlet. The anterior shoulder escapes the symphysis pubis while the posterior shoulder sweeps the perineum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="external-rotation-of-the-head">External Rotation of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-rotation-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As the internal rotation of the shoulders takes place, the head, which has already been born, rotates 1/8 of a circle as in restitution. The head now lies in the lateral position.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="external-rotation-of-the-head">External rotation of the head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-rotation-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-005795bb.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lateral-flexion">Lateral Flexion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lateral-flexion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Following these movements the body bends sideways to follow the curve of the birth canal. The anterior shoulder escapes under the symphysis pubis and the posterior shoulder sweeps the perineum. The body of the baby is born by lateral flexion.</p>
<p>To recap, the cardinal movements of labour in a vertex presentation are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Engagement</li>
<li>Descent</li>
<li>Flexion</li>
<li>Internal rotation</li>
<li>Extension</li>
<li>External restitution of the head</li>
<li>Expulsion</li>
</ol>
<p>An easy way to remember these movements is by use of the mnemonic device - 'Every Decent Family In Europe Eats Eggs'.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-the-second-stage-of-normal-labour">Management of the Second Stage of Normal Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-the-second-stage-of-normal-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before you begin, try to remember the probable signs of the second stage of labour. Write them down on a piece of paper.</p>
<ul>
<li>Expulsive uterine contraction. This may happen in occipital posterior or when the head is deeply engaged with fully loaded rectum (in a case where the mother is not in second stage)</li>
<li>A trickle of blood</li>
<li>There may be no bleeding while the cervix is fully dilated</li>
<li>Pouting and gaping of the anus</li>
<li>Gaping of the vulva in primigravida. The vulva of multiparous will gape even in premature pushing</li>
<li>Tenseness between the anus and coccyx</li>
<li>Bulging of the perineum usually means delivery is imminent</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-the-second-stage-of-normal-labour">Management of the Second Stage of Normal Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-the-second-stage-of-normal-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-recall-the-equipment-you-will-need-during-the-second-stage-of-labour">Can you recall the equipment you will need during the second stage of labour?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-recall-the-equipment-you-will-need-during-the-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will need a trolley with a top and bottom shelf.</p>
<p>On the top shelf make sure you have:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sterile delivery pack</li>
<li>Small bucket with 0.5% jik for decontaminating instruments</li>
<li>Bucket with 0.5% jik for decontaminating linen</li>
<li>A bucket with plastic bag for used swabs and gloves</li>
</ul>
<p>On the bottom shelf you should have the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Suturing pack</li>
<li>Antiseptic solution</li>
<li>Draw sheet and mackintosh</li>
<li>Syntocinon drawn, in a receiver</li>
<li>Lignocaine</li>
<li>5% dextrose solution 500mls</li>
<li>Needles</li>
<li>Branulars</li>
<li>Syringes (for emergency)</li>
<li>Sterile gloves</li>
</ul>
<p>The following steps are suggested in the management of the second stage of labour:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the procedure to the mother and reassure her</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Ask your assistant to open and arrange the delivery pack while you scrub up</li>
<li>Gown and glove yourself methodically</li>
<li>Instruct your assistant to put the patient in the dorsal position</li>
<li>Swab the mother methodically</li>
<li>Lubricate your two fingers and perform vaginal examination to confirm second stage</li>
<li>You should also instruct your assistant to check the foetal heart beat after every contraction, the mother's pulse after every ten minutes and to administer syntometrin after the delivery of the anterior shoulder</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-75e08df2.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg">
Flexing of the head and guarding of the perineum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-management-of-the-second-stage-of-labour">The Management of the Second Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-management-of-the-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Tell the patient to wait for a contraction. When it comes, she should take in a full breath, close her mouth and bear down as strongly as she can, then quickly take in another breath and bear down again.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>She should be able to make at least two efforts during each contraction and relax between contractions. Encourage her all the time and explain the progress being made towards the birth of her baby.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place the baby towel on the bed, with the scissors and two forceps for clamping the cord. Prepare two pieces of cotton wool for wiping the newborn's eyes, some gauze for cleaning the airway and for a covering when cutting the cord.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At this stage the head might start distending the perineum. The anus starts dilating and the head is seen at the vulva. It keeps receding between contractions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When the head distends the perineum check if the perineum is stretching well.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place the left hand on the advancing head with fingers spread equally over the vertex towards the bregma to stop any sudden explosive effort during and after crowning of the head. With the right hand guard the perineum, holding it with the pad.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check if the perineum is stretching. If not, give an episiotomy at the height of a contraction if there is any indication that the head is about to crown.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="crowning-of-the-head">Crowning of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#crowning-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Next is the crowning of the head. The parietal eminences pass through the bony outlet. At this stage the head no longer recedes between contractions.</p>
<p>Tell the mother to stop pushing as this might lead to a rapid delivery of the head and consequent brain damage. Ask her to pant. Research has shown that a series of short pushes are more effective than a long push. Encourage her as she pushes.</p>
<p>It is really hard work! So keep encouraging the mother with kind words and warmth!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="extension-of-the-head">Extension of the head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extension-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Assist the extension by grasping the parietal eminences with your left hand. Let the head come out slowly and naturally. Feel for the cord around the baby's neck. If it is there, slip it from the baby's neck over the head. If it is too tight, place two artery forceps on the cord and cut it between them. When the nose and mouth come out, wipe away the mucus with a sterile swab. By this point the whole head should be out.</p>
<p>The head will have restituted and rotated spontaneously to face the mother's left or right thigh. This shows you that the shoulders have descended and rotated to the anterior posterior diameter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="delivering-the-shoulders-by-lateral-flexion-of-the-body">Delivering the Shoulders by Lateral Flexion of the Body<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delivering-the-shoulders-by-lateral-flexion-of-the-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when delivering the shoulders by lateral flexion of the body:</p>
<ul>
<li>Place one hand above and one below the foetal head</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Depress the head gently toward the anus/neck, making sure it is neither twisted nor bent sideways till the anterior shoulder is free</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-6cf70649.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg">
The delivering of anterior shoulder</p>
<p>â˜ Remind your assistant to give syntometrine 0.5mg intramuscularly (in a single dose)
â˜ Guide the head upwards in the direction of the mother's abdomen</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-6e16a488.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg">
The delivering of posterior shoulder</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The posterior shoulder will escape smoothly over the perineum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The rest of the body will be born by lateral flexion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask your assistant for the time and note the time of birth</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place the baby at a slight slant to drain the mucous</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Put the baby on the baby towel, clamp and cut the cord</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give the APGAR score to the baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Show the baby to the mother to identify the sex of the baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask your assistant to continue with the immediate care of the baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continue with the delivery of the placenta by using control cord traction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check the placenta for completeness and/or malformation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Measure blood loss</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do the first examination of the baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weigh the baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do a post natal examination and record all the findings</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give the mother a hot drink and transfer her to the postnatal ward</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="apgar-score">APGAR Score<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#apgar-score" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Can you remember how to give an APGAR score?</p>
<p>Once the baby is out into the world, your work has just begun. You will need to assess the baby periodically.</p>
<p>After delivering the baby, an assessment of the general condition is done after one minute and again after five minutes. This involves the consideration of five specific signs and the degree to which they are present or absent. The factors assessed are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Appearance - Colour</li>
<li>Pulse - Heart rate</li>
<li>Grimace - good grimace</li>
<li>Activity - Muscle tone</li>
<li>Respiratory efforts â€“ vigorous crying</li>
</ul>
<p>A score of 0, 1, 2 is awarded to each of these signs in accordance with the APGAR Score Chart.</p>
<p>APGAR Score Chart</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Sign</th><th>Score 0</th><th>Score1</th><th>Score2</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Appearance</td><td>Pale or blue</td><td>Body pink, extremities blue</td><td>Pink all over</td></tr><tr><td>Pulse/heart rate</td><td>Absent</td><td>Less than 100/min</td><td>More than 100/min</td></tr><tr><td>Grimace</td><td>None</td><td>Slight</td><td>Good</td></tr><tr><td>Activity (tone)</td><td>Limp</td><td>Some flexion/movement</td><td>Spontaneous movements/active</td></tr><tr><td>Respiratory effort</td><td>None</td><td>Weak or slow/gasping</td><td>Good/vigorous cry</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>A normal infant in good condition at birth will achieve an APGAR score of 7 to 10. A score of 0 to 3 is severe birth asphyxia and 4 to 6 is moderate birth asphyxia, both of which require immediate resuscitation of the baby. Immediate Care of the Baby</p>
<p>Clear the airways by sucking mucus from the mouth and nostrils and give oxygen if necessary. Ligate the cord and make sure the ligature is very tight before you cut the cord. Wipe the baby's head and the body and wrap to keep warm. You should record the following information about the baby:</p>
<ul>
<li>Label the baby with the mother's name and
I.P. number</li>
<li>Write the date and time of delivery</li>
<li>Sex of the baby</li>
<li>Birth weight</li>
</ul>
<p>After handing the baby over to your assistant, you will have to continue to deliver the placenta using control cord traction. At this point you should remind yourself about the process of the third stage labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-the-third-stage-of-labour">Principles of the Third Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-the-third-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="mechanism-of-the-third-stage-of-labour-physiology-of-third-stage">Mechanism of the Third Stage of Labour Physiology of Third Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-the-third-stage-of-labour-physiology-of-third-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Assuming that all the aforementioned factors are well taken care of, you will now look at the physiology of the third stage of labour, starting with the mechanical factors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-mechanical-factors">The Mechanical Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-mechanical-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>During the third stage, the following mechanical factors come into play:</p>
<ul>
<li>The uterus reduces in size 2.5cm below the umbilicus, or 15cm above the symphysis pubis after the expulsion of the foetus</li>
<li>The contraction and retraction of the uterine muscles continues</li>
<li>The placental site is reduced to half</li>
<li>Since the placenta is inelastic, it does not contract, so it detaches from the shrinking uterine wall</li>
<li>The placenta is pushed further to the lower uterine segment by the weight of the retro-placental clot. This is the</li>
</ul>
<p>accumulated blood from the separated placenta</p>
<ul>
<li>With the next contraction the placenta is pushed into the vagina and expelled</li>
</ul>
<p>You will know that the placenta has separated and has been expelled from the upper uterine segment into the lower segment or into the vagina when you have noted:</p>
<ul>
<li>Elongation of the cord which does not recede on pressing at the symphysis pubis</li>
<li>A gush of blood</li>
<li>The uterus contracts like a cricket ball.</li>
</ul>
<p>The placenta is expelled either with maternal side exposed, known as the Mathew-Duncan method or the foetal side exposed known as the Shultz Method.</p>
<p>Click here to view the Mathew Duncan method.</p>
<p>Click here to view the Shultz method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-of-bleeding">Control of Bleeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-of-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following steps should be taken to ensure the control of bleeding:</p>
<ul>
<li>The uterine muscle's contraction and retraction causes the placental site to reduce into half. Criss-cross fibres control bleeding by compressing the blood vessels. These fibres are also known as 'living ligatures'</li>
<li>Clotting of blood takes place in the sinuses sealing the bleeding points a few hours later when uterine contractions are less vigorous.</li>
</ul>
<p>The time interval between the delivery of the baby and delivery of the placenta is a dangerous period, in which one of the greatest complications of pregnancy and labour can occur.</p>
<p>This complication is excessive bleeding or postpartum haemorrhage (PPH). You should never leave the mother alone even for a short while during this stage.</p>
<p>The third stage of labour can be managed either passively or actively. You will now study each of these two modes of management in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-passive-or-natural-method-of-managing-the-third">The Passive or Natural Method of Managing the Third<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-passive-or-natural-method-of-managing-the-third" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-labour">Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The passive or natural method occurs naturally, that is without any interference. For example, in a normal delivery, if oxytocic drugs are not used, the uterus generally remains inactive for a few minutes after the delivery of the baby, after</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>which regular contractions then begin again. Physiology of the third stage takes place, the placenta is expelled and bleeding is controlled.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="giving-oxytocic-drugs">Giving Oxytocic Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#giving-oxytocic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Oxytocin, ergometrine or syntometrine stimulate uterine contraction. Ergometrine 0.5mg given IM causes a uterine contraction to occur five to seven minutes after the injection. Given intravenously it acts within 45 seconds. Syntometrine is a mixture of oxytocin and ergometrine 0.5ml given IM acts within two to three minutes. Usually sytrometrine is given with the delivery of the anterior shoulder while ergometrine is given at the crowning of the head.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="controlled-cord-traction">Controlled Cord Traction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#controlled-cord-traction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The uterus must be firmly contracted before this method can be used. It is not necessary to wait for signs of placenta separation. Place the left hand above the symphysis pubis, push the uterus upwards and backwards with the right hand and pull the cord downwards and outwards. Apply traction steadily without jerking, see the illustration on the right. When the placenta is visible at the vulva, direct the cord upwards. The placenta will follow the curve of the birth canal. Receive it with both hands and rotate the placenta. This will twist the membranes. You can then deliver the membranes with up side movements, which enable them to be drawn out without breaking.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-effort">Maternal Effort<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-effort" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is not commonly used. When the placenta has separated and descended, the palm is placed downwards on the mother's abdomen to provide a backup that the mother can push against. During a contraction, the mother should be asked to push down. The placenta will be pushed out of the vagina. This method is useful in the event of a macerated birth</p>
<p>Do not apply downward fundal pressure while doing cord traction as this can lead to inversion of the uterus.</p>
<p>The other method that can be used to deliver the placenta is the fundal pressure method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fundal-pressure">Fundal Pressure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fundal-pressure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method should be used in case of a macerated or pre-term baby as the strength of the cord is reduced. You should wait for the following signs of placental separation:</p>
<ul>
<li>The fundus feels hard like a cricket ball</li>
<li>There is a gush of blood due to placenta separation</li>
<li>The cord lengthens and doesn't recede with pressure on the symphysis pubis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Make sure the bladder is empty. Instruct the mother to breathe through an open mouth slowly and quietly. When there is a contraction, grasp the uterus with your left hand fingers behind the uterus. Thumb in the anterior surface. Apply pressure to the pelvic inlet in downward and backward direction. Receive the placenta with both hands. If the membranes do not slip out, turn the placenta around and deliver the membranes slowly with an upward movement. Rub the uterus and expel the clots.</p>
<p>Once the placenta is out, you will need to examine the birth canal.</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain to the mother that you need to check if she has any tears, warn her it will be a bit painful but the worst part has passed, you will be very gentle and quick and that she needs to cooperate</li>
<li>Change the gloves, roll gauze over pointing and middle fingers of the right hand</li>
<li>Insert middle fingers of left hand facing upwards pushing the upper vaginal wall</li>
<li>With the right hand press down the lower vaginal wall exposing the cervix</li>
<li>Check the cervix for bleeding, oedema or tears</li>
<li>Check for any tears with the two fingers of your right hand, mop both sides of the vaginal wall, finish with the fourchette</li>
<li>Reassure the mother in case there is any tear for suturing</li>
<li>Cover the perineum with the folded pad into a half</li>
<li>Wipe the buttocks from the fourchette towards the rectum cover the perineum completely</li>
<li>Collect any blood loss from the bed</li>
<li>Change the bed linen with the help of an assistant</li>
<li>In case of episiotomy or a tear, scrub your hands while your assistant is</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>setting a sterile suturing pack and repair the tear</p>
<ul>
<li>Ask the mother to lie on her back with her legs crossed on each other</li>
<li>Ask the assistant to hand over the baby to the mother</li>
<li>Leave the mother to rest while you go to examine the placenta</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Write down any reasons you can think of, for examining the placenta.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="you-now-know-why-we-examine-the-placenta-but-how-do-you-go-about-it">You now know why we examine the placenta. But how do you go about it?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#you-now-know-why-we-examine-the-placenta-but-how-do-you-go-about-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-fourth-stage-of-labour">The Fourth Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-fourth-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fourth stage starts after the delivery of the placenta and lasts for one hour. The nurse or midwife should observe the mother for blood loss, monitor vital signs, reassure her and let the mother hold the baby. The nurse should also record notes in the patients file, fill in the baby notification form and after the hour is over escort the mother to the maternity unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examination-of-the-baby">Examination of the Baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As mentioned earlier, once the baby is delivered, a thorough first examination is done. Can you remember at what time interval?</p>
<p>A thorough physical examination is done one hour after birth with the aim of assessing maturity and excluding obvious congenital abnormalities and injuries at birth. In order to carry out this examination, you need to have with you the following equipment in a tray:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tape measure</li>
<li>Second hand watch</li>
<li>Gloves</li>
<li>Weighing scale</li>
<li>Clinical thermometer</li>
<li>Lubricant</li>
<li>Swabs</li>
<li>Stethoscope</li>
</ul>
<p>Examine the baby systematically in the following manner:</p>
<ul>
<li>Vital signs - heart rate (120-160/min), respiration (20-60 average 44/min), and temperature (36-37 degrees centigrade).</li>
<li>Head - Check the shape to see if there is excessive moulding, caput succedaneum or depressed fractures to exclude head injury, microcephalus or hydrocephalus. Take head circumference (Approximately 33-37 cm).</li>
<li>Ears - Check position. If they are low set, this may indicate Down's syndrome or Mongolism. Check for any missing lobes or cartilage.</li>
<li>Eyes - Check for presence of eyeball injuries, discharge or jaundice.</li>
<li>Mouth - Check for harelip, cleft palate, tongue-tie or false teeth, septic spots, thrush, cysts.</li>
<li>Nostrils - Check for patency with no polyps or flaring.</li>
<li>Neck - Check for congenital goitre or enlarged glands.</li>
<li>Upper limbs - Check for equality, free movement, fractures, webbed fingers, extra digits and any bony tissues. Extra digits can be ligated with silk and will fall off (with the parents permission). Check for Erb's palsy.</li>
<li>Chest - Check for continuity of sternum and the shape of rib-cage, respiratory rate, enlarged breast or absence of breast tissue.</li>
<li>Abdomen - Should be intact and firm, check for umbilical hernia and exomphalus (protrusion of abdominal organs through a defect in the anterior wall). Abdominal distension is present in hydrops foetalis. Check for blood oozing from the cord and clamp again if necessary (cord shrivels within 24 hours, falls off 6-10 days).</li>
<li>External genitalia - Confirm the sex of the baby to rule out pseudo-haemophrodism or intersexes. In males check for undescended testes, hypo/hyperspadias and phimosis. In females, check for bleeding from urethral and vaginal orifice. Vaginal bleeding may be due to excessive hormones from the mother</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neurological-assessment">Neurological Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurological-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This entails the checking of reflexes, which deal with the function of the baby's nervous system as well as physical and behavioural assessments. At the beginning of the examination, observe the baby's movements. These movements involve all extremities and should be random and symmetrical but never stereotyped. Sometimes jitteriness or tremors will be noted. The first time you notice these movements they may look like fits. To determine the difference between the two, hold the affected limb. If it is the former the tremors should stop.</p>
<p>Neurological assessments include the following, click the links to reveal the details of each:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="moro-reflex">Moro Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moro-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Support the baby's head and body in supine position about a centimetre from the cot. Allow the head to drop back. Look at the baby's response. The baby throws out his arms extending the elbows and fingers with embracing movements of the arms. What is the significance of the Moro reflex?</p>
<p>The Moro reflex is symmetrical in a normal baby at birth and disappears after three months. It is incomplete in the pre-term baby and absent in the baby with inter cranial drainage. If brain damage is not severe it returns after three to four days. If it disappears some hours after birth, you should then suspect increasing cerebral oedema or slow intra cranial haemorrhage.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-13e37553.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tonic-neck-reflex">Tonic Neck Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tonic-neck-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A fencing position is assumed, that is, the baby lies on the back, head rotated to one side with one arm and leg partially or completely extended. The opposite arm and leg are flexed. This is a manifestation of the immaturity of the newborn's nervous system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rooting-reflex">Rooting Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rooting-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To test for the rooting reflex, gently touch the corner of the baby's mouth with clean fingers. The baby will open his mouth turning towards the stimulus in anticipation of the mother's nipple. To check for sucking reflex place a clean finger in the baby's mouth noting the sucking strength. The sucking reflex is poor in pre-term babies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stepping-reflex">Stepping Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stepping-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The stepping or dancing reflex is present at birth but disappears soon after. Once this reflex diminishes, the infant does not attempt a stepping motion until he/she starts to walk. Hold the infant up, with the feet touching a surface. The infant will attempt to make some steps or pressing movements.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="grasp-reflex">Grasp Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#grasp-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is amusing to learn that a newborn baby can grasp. At birth, the grasping reflex of both hands and feet is present. The infant will grasp any object you place in their hand, and then let it go. They are able to hold on to a finger so securely, that you can lift them to a standing position. Stroking the soles of the feet causes the toes to turn downwards trying to grasp. By applying traction to the baby's wrists raise them to a sitting position. A full term infant will offer a strong resistance while a pre-term does not resist the pull.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protective-reflex">Protective Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protective-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Other reflexes include protective reflexes such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>The blinking reflex, which protects the eyes from bright light</li>
<li>Sneezing and coughing reflexes used to clear the infant's throat</li>
<li>The yawn reflex, which draws additional oxygen</li>
<li>Cry reflex, which helps to withdraw from painful stimuli</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 114 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>All of these reflexes either diminish or strengthen as need be, influencing behaviour patterns, which become more complex.</p>
<p>Once this examination is completed, the baby can be placed on the cot for transfer to the nursery or given to the mother.</p>
<p>After completing the delivery of the baby, you should transfer the mother to the postnatal ward where she will rest.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiology-of-third-stage">Physiology of Third Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiology-of-third-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>What changes take place in a woman who has just delivered during puerperium?</p>
<p>The puerperium period covers six to eight weeks following delivery or abortion and is characterised by:</p>
<ul>
<li>General organs return to their pre-gravida state</li>
<li>Initiation of lactation</li>
<li>Recuperation</li>
</ul>
<p>Have you talked to friends about how they felt during their puerperal period? You will be surprised! Some say that whenever the midwife asked them any questions, they felt irritated for no good reason. Others felt like crying when their partners were late to visit. Some felt like screaming when the baby cried and wanted to cover it with a pillow to suffocate the innocent precious baby!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-psychology-of-the-mother-during-puerperium">The Psychology of the Mother During Puerperium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-psychology-of-the-mother-during-puerperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the puerperium the mother is subjected to emotional turmoil and you must be supportive and observant. She should be allowed to cuddle her baby and express her love as she wishes. This maternal instinct is at times delayed.</p>
<p>The midwife should be kind, patient, and compassionate towards the mother and give her the necessary education concerning her and the baby. Each mother should be taken as an individual based on her maternal experience, educational background, maturity and parity. Mothers should be given all the information necessary to ensure they know how to care for their babies.</p>
<p>Rooming is the term given when a hospital plans for the mother to stay with the baby for most of the 24 hours in a day. It is highly recommended because it has been seen to have great psychological advantages for both mother and baby. Bonding commences immediately and demand breast-feeding can be successfully practised. Most baby-friendly hospitals in this country encourage rooming in.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="postpartum-tears-or-fourth-day-blues">Postpartum Tears or Fourth Day Blues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postpartum-tears-or-fourth-day-blues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This condition is characterised by mild depression and mood swings due to a temporary endocrine hormonal imbalance following childbirth. It occurs in fifty percent of post-natal mothers on around the fourth day. A midwife should try to prevent the 'blues' by educating the mother during the pre-natal period on how to take care of herself and the baby to build up her confidence. Involve the partner in these teachings so that the partner can give moral support. Teach the mother how to check for minor discomfort and the relevant remedies to reduce the feeling of anxiety that the baby is ill whenever they cry.</p>
<p>It is a time of great physiological change, accompanied by some anatomical and psychological changes as well. This is a time of change in the body in general with the exception of the breasts.</p>
<p>The breasts continue to develop so as to establish and maintain lactation.</p>
<p>The other changes that take place in the mother are outlined on the following pages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-involution">General Involution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-involution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Every system in the body is affected during this process, including the heart and circulatory system. With the cessation of the utero-placental circulation, the work done by the heart decreases. The quantity of blood required also gradually returns to normal. The renal and musculo-skeletal systems also return to normal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="involution-of-the-uterus">Involution of the Uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#involution-of-the-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The size of the pregnant uterus is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>30</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>22</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>20</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30 \times 22 \times 20\mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">30</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">22</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">20</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span> and it weighs 100gms at the end of labour. It is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>15</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>11</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>7.5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">15 \times 11 \times 7.5\mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">15</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">11</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">7.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span> by the end of puerperium. Involution takes place, by which point it measures <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>7.5</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>5</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>2.5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">7.5 \times 5 \times 2.5\mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">7.5</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span> and weighs 60gms. Involution is the return of the uterus to its normal size, position and tone and is brought about by autolysis</p>
<p>and ischaemia.</p>
<p>Autolysis is a process by which muscle fibres are digested by the proteolytic hormone. The muscle fibres have to dissolve a large amount of their protein in order to achieve this reduction in size. This means that a great deal of nitrogen is excreted by the body in the urine together with the excess fluid retained during pregnancy. This is why a lot of urine containing large amounts of nitrogen is excreted during the first few days after delivery. In addition, the epithelial lining of</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>the uterus, other cellular debris, and red blood cells are expelled as lochia from the uterus.</p>
<p>Ischaemia is localised anaemia of the uterus, which occurs when the placenta is expelled. Blood vessels are constricted, which results in the reduction of the blood supply to the uterus. The phagocytes dispose of the redundant muscle fibre and elastic tissue. The vagina, ligaments of the uterus and muscle of the pelvis also return to their pre-gravida state. If not, prolapse of the uterus may occur later.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="onset-of-lactation">Onset of Lactation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#onset-of-lactation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lowered oestrogen levels trigger the production of prolactin from the anterior pituitary gland, which initiates lactation. The maintenance of lactation depends on putting the baby on the breast, but secretion of milk commences on the third to fourth day. The baby should be put on the breast immediately, which leads to oxytocin release and assists in keeping the uterus well-contracted. (You should revise the anatomy and physiology of the breast in unit one).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-normal-puerperium">Management of Normal Puerperium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-normal-puerperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The aim of managing the puerperium is to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain the mother's good health</li>
<li>Aid involution of the pelvic area</li>
<li>Promote breast-feeding</li>
<li>Prevent infection and other puerperium complications</li>
<li>Educate the mother on the proper care of her own health and the baby</li>
</ul>
<p>The mother and the baby should be examined daily and if any abnormality is noted, the doctor should be informed. When noting the mother's general condition, you should check for the following points:</p>
<ul>
<li>Assess happiness, sadness, worries and fears and address them appropriately.</li>
<li>Ambulation is important to prevent deep venous thrombosis.</li>
<li>Take her temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure twice daily.</li>
<li>Check the breasts and if she is not lactating, express colostrum.</li>
<li>Increase expressing on the second day and milk should be established on the fourth day.</li>
<li>Advise the mother on how to feed the infant. When fixing the baby on the</li>
</ul>
<p>breast she should put the whole areola in the baby's mouth.</p>
<ul>
<li>She should initially breast feed the baby for three minutes to prevent cracked nipples and empty the breast in cases where the baby does not feed a lot. This is especially important in the first days to prevent engorgement.</li>
</ul>
<p>Measure the fundal height and record the measurement daily. Assess whether the involution is taking place satisfactory. The fundal height should reduce by 0.5 - 1 centimetre daily. Check on lochia loss, noting the colour. This should change as per the schedule we noted earlier. If there is persistent red lochia, this points to the need for further investigation. Offensive lochia odour denotes infection.</p>
<p>You should also check the perineum to see if there was episiotomy and note its state. Advise the mother to wash the episiotomy at least four times a day with salt water and change the pad as soon as it is soiled and after she goes to the toilet.</p>
<p>Check on the calf muscles and exclude any pain that may indicate deep venous thrombosis. You should also exclude oedema and anaemia. Ensure that the mother gets enough sleep and rest. If she cannot sleep, she should be given a sedative.</p>
<p>Take note of any pain and administer analgesics. Ask the mother to report if lochia is heavy. Also encourage her to pass urine when her bladder is full. Encourage her to continuously check on the baby's cord and to report any bleeding, especially in the first 12 hours.</p>
<p>Measure the fundal height and record the measurement daily. Assess whether the involution is taking place satisfactory. The fundal height should reduce by 0.5 - 1 centimetre daily. Check on lochia loss, noting the colour. This should change as per the schedule we noted earlier. If there is persistent red lochia, this points to the need for further investigation. Offensive lochia odour denotes infection.</p>
<p>You should also check the perineum to see if there was episiotomy and note its state. Advise the mother to wash the episiotomy at least four times a day with salt water and change the pad as soon as it is soiled and after she goes to the toilet.</p>
<p>Check on the calf muscles and exclude any pain that may indicate deep venous thrombosis. You should also exclude oedema and anaemia. Ensure that the mother gets enough sleep and</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>rest. If she cannot sleep, she should be given a sedative.</p>
<p>Take note of any pain and administer analgesics. Ask the mother to report if lochia is heavy. Also encourage her to pass urine when her bladder is full. Encourage her to continuously check on the baby's cord and to report any bleeding, especially in the first 12 hours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-think-of-any-minor-and-major-complications-of-puerperium">Can you think of any minor and major complications of puerperium?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-of-any-minor-and-major-complications-of-puerperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="major-complications">Major Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#major-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Venous thrombosis</li>
<li>Pulmonary embolism</li>
<li>Retention of urine or retention with overflow</li>
<li>Urinary tract infection</li>
<li>Puerperal sepsis and pyrexia</li>
<li>Engorgement of the breasts</li>
<li>Cracked nipples or mastitis</li>
<li>Puerperal psychosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="minor-complications">Minor complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#minor-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
