<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-natal-examination">Post Natal Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-natal-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is carried out during the sixth post-partum week. You should inquire about the general health of the mother and baby. You should also do a haemoglobin estimate and if you find that it is low, embark on treatment.</p>
<p>You should inquire and note any gynaecological symptoms. Examine the mother's general condition, with specific emphasis on the breasts. Find out if the breasts are active. Examine the abdomen for tone of muscle and any masses. Also examine the vulva and vagina to ascertain the healing of the repaired episiotomy or tear. Pass a speculum (sims) to see the state of the cervix and if there is any discharge. Do a Pap smear at this stage. If possible, you should carry out a bimanual examination of the uterus to ascertain that the uterus has involuted to its normal size. Finally, remind the mother of the various family planning methods discussed and re-emphasise the importance of attending maternal and child health clinics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-the-neonate">SECTION 2: THE NEONATE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-the-neonate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this section you will focus on the new life, that is the neonate, who is now an independent being outside the mother's womb.</p>
<p>'Neo' means, new, hence the term 'neonate' means newborn.</p>
<p>The neonatal period is the first four weeks after birth. A neonate can be classified as, preterm, full term or post term.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section, you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the physiology of the neonate</li>
<li>Explain the care of the neonate</li>
<li>Describe the management of the high risk neonate</li>
<li>Describe the management of a neonate with abnormal conditions</li>
<li>Describe the management of neonatal emergencies</li>
<li>Describe the management of birth traumas</li>
<li>Describe the management of congenital abnormalities</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="physiology-of-the-newborn">Physiology of the Newborn<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiology-of-the-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Knowledge on the physiology of a newborn is necessary to ensure appropriate care of the neonate. In the first section of this unit, you learnt about the management of the second stage of labour and the examination you should carry out on the newborn baby.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="try-to-think-of-three-main-physiological-adjustments-in-a-neonate-at-birth">Try to think of three main physiological adjustments in a neonate at birth.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#try-to-think-of-three-main-physiological-adjustments-in-a-neonate-at-birth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Immediately at birth, there are three main adjustments that take place involving the lungs, the cardiovascular system and the temperature regulating centre to allow for the independent existence of the newborn baby.</p>
<p>You will now look at each of these adjustments in turn starting with those involving the respiratory system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="changes-in-the-lungs">Changes in the Lungs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#changes-in-the-lungs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The onset of respiration in a newborn confirms life. The start of pulmonary respiration is due to physiological and mechanical reasons. Lack of oxygen and high levels of carbon dioxide in the</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>circulation occur when placental circulation ceases. This stimulates the respiratory centre in the medulla to initiate normal respiration.</p>
<p>Mechanically, respiration is stimulated when the chest wall, which was compressed during the passage of the baby in the birth canal, allows the fluid to drain from the lungs. Consequently, the cool air on the baby's face and handling during birth will stimulate the baby to cry as soon as they are born. After the baby takes in their first breath, the blood vessels in the lungs expand to initiate respiration.</p>
<p>At first the baby's breathing may be rapid and irregular. It is mainly abnormal at a rate of 40 - 50 respirations per minute.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="circulatory-changes">Circulatory Changes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#circulatory-changes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will recall that in unit two you studied foetal circulation. If you have forgotten what you covered, please refer to that section again. In summary, you noted that:</p>
<ul>
<li>Foetal type of circulation ceases as the respiration commences</li>
<li>Normal circulation starts when the temporary structures stop functioning</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-5611e6f5.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-four-temporary-structures-in-foetal-circulation">What are the four temporary structures in foetal circulation?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-four-temporary-structures-in-foetal-circulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>I hope you thought of the following structures:</p>
<ul>
<li>Foramen ovale</li>
<li>Ductus arteriosus</li>
<li>Ductus venosus</li>
<li>Umbilical vein and hypogastric arteries</li>
</ul>
<p>As the placental circulation ceases soon after birth when the umbilical cord is ligated, the blood flow to the right side of the heart decreases and the blood on the left side increases causing the foreman ovale to close.</p>
<p>With the establishment of pulmonary respiration, the ductus arteries close. Complete closure happens within eight to ten hours of birth.</p>
<p>The cessation of placental circulation will result in the collapse and subsequently drying of the umbilical veins, the ductus venosus and the hypogastric arteries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Persistence or reopening of the ductus may occur if pulmonary vascular resistance is high. Cyanosis or cyanotic attacks will be evident as a result. This is a common problem of preterm neonates with Respiratory Distress Syndrome.</p>
<p>Anatomical closure by fibrous tissue occurs within two to three months, resulting in the formation of the ligamentum teres, ligamentum venosum and obliterated hypogastric arteries.</p>
<p>Cardiopulmonary adaptations, which take place at birth, are interdependent. This means that failure to establish respiration and satisfactory tissue oxygenation presents a life threatening situation to the neonate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thermo-heat-regulation">Thermo (Heat) Regulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thermo-heat-regulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The neonate leaves a thermo constant environment</p>
<p>of 37.1 degrees Celsius, where they have survived</p>
<p>for nine months and enters a much cooler atmosphere at delivery. This affects the neonate in</p>
<p>various ways.</p>
<p>Firstly, heat regulation in the neonate is poor because of their inefficient heat regulating centre.</p>
<p>The subcutaneous fat layer of the neonate is thin and provides poor insulation, allowing the transfer of core</p>
<p>heat to the environment and also cooling of the baby's blood. In addition to evaporation, further heat</p>
<p>will be lost by conduction when the baby is in contact with cold surfaces, by radiation to cold objects in the environment and by convection caused by currents of cool air passing over the surface of their body. Incidences of the latter may be substantially increased by air</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>conditioning systems in some of our modern delivery rooms. Since the neonate's temperature regulating centres are not very efficient, there is a risk of either overheating or chilling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-physiological-changes-in-a-newborn">Other Physiological Changes In a Newborn<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-physiological-changes-in-a-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In addition to the three physiological changes discussed above there are other changes that occur as described below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="liver-function">Liver Function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liver-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Physiological jaundice is usually seen in 50% of normal neonates from the third to the sixth day of life. This is due to excessive break down of red blood cells resulting from a high haemoglobin level (Hb of 14 - 18mgs/100mls).</p>
<p>The process of breaking down red blood cells leads to formation of bilirubin. The liver is not able to conjugate the excess bilirubin to enable its secretion through the kidneys. This leads to jaundice. You will see more details on conjugation later in this section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="digestion">Digestion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#digestion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The neonate is capable of passing the first stool, known as meconium, within the first two to three days of life. This is because the foetus swallows liquor amnii in utero. Thus, their sucking and swallowing reflexes are usually present at birth.</p>
<p>The colour of the meconium is dark greenish and later changes to a mustard (yellowish) colour. The bowels may be opened three to five times daily.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="weight">Weight<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#weight" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The average normal birth weight ranges from 2.5 - 3.5 kilograms. During the first three days of life, the baby loses approximately 10 - 20% of their birth weight but regains it again within one to two weeks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-two-possible-reasons-for-weight-loss-in-a-newborn">What are two possible reasons for weight loss in a newborn?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-two-possible-reasons-for-weight-loss-in-a-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Your answer should include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Due to tissue fluid loss during the heat loss when the baby is born</li>
<li>When the baby opens their bowels, the meconium which was present in the gut is lost, leading to weight reduction</li>
<li>Poor sucking on the breast due to tiredness incurred during the baby's passage through the birth canal during labour will affect the baby's weight since they are not getting enough fluid intake</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skin">Skin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The skin of a newborn is covered with vernix caseosa in utero to protect and help retain heat and also act as a lubricant during delivery.</p>
<p>The sebaceous glands cease to produce vernix after birth, which may lead to dryness of the skin. The vernix caseosa will peel off within three days of delivery if left alone. There is also plenty of fine hair (lanugo) on the skin which falls off in the first month of life.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="care-of-a-newborn">Care of a Newborn<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-a-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Neonatal care is designed to provide an environment conducive to the well being of the baby and to prevent complications.</p>
<p>As a midwife, you should realise that the neonatal period is a very hazardous period. Statistics show that two thirds of infantile deaths occur in the neonatal period. More than half of these deaths occur in the first 48 hours and three quarters in the first week of life.</p>
<p>Therefore, the midwife's responsibility is to minimise these deaths through efficient management of the infant.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immediate-care-of-a-newborn">Immediate Care of a Newborn<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immediate-care-of-a-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the delivery of the baby's head, excess mucus may be wiped gently from the mouth.</p>
<p>Immediately the baby is born, they should be held slanting with the head at a lower angle for a short period to allow drainage of mucus and liquor amnii, which may have been swallowed.</p>
<p>The baby is stimulated to cry in order to take its first breath (refer to the discussion on management in the second stage of labour).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Gentle handling while stimulating the baby to cry during delivery is essential. The practice before was to hold baby upside down and vigorously hit the soles of the feet. However, this causes injuries to the internal organs and also means a lot of pressure is applied to the chest cavity because all organs gravitate down when the baby is held upside down.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-810b8a4b.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-104e7be2.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<p>The baby is laid across the mother's abdomen as the cord is clamped, ligated and cut. The timing of the clamping of the cord is not crucial unless asphyxia, prematurity or rhesus incompatibility is present.</p>
<p>Wrap the baby with a towel and place them in a warm cot with their head to one side. The head should be lower than the body in order for the secretions to drain and not block the airway. Ensure that the baby has an identification wristlet, which should be put on before the baby leaves the delivery couch/bed.</p>
<p>Leave the baby to rest for an hour in order to recuperate from the strain of labour and birth. Frequent observations should be made during this period to ensure that the baby's respiration is normal, and that they are not bleeding or haemorrhaging from the cord.</p>
<p>The first examination of the newborn is performed after one hour.</p>
<p>Assessment of the newborn is done by scoring at one minute after birth. Repeat at five minutes and then ten minutes. This is known as the APGAR score. Can you remember how to score the baby?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="try-to-write-down-four-vital-signs-that-are-assessed-in-the-apgar-scoring">Try to write down four vital signs that are assessed in the APGAR scoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#try-to-write-down-four-vital-signs-that-are-assessed-in-the-apgar-scoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In 1953, Dr Virginia Apgar designed a chart which gives an index of the infant's degree of depression (if any) at birth, determining their need for help through five easily observed signs: heart rate, respiratory effort, muscle tone, reflex response, and colour. These five vital signs are each given a score of 0, 1 or 2 points.</p>
<p>Each vital sign is represented by a letter, forming the word APGAR that is:</p>
<p>A Appearance
A Activity
P Pulse or apex beat
R Respiration
G Grimace</p>
<p>Have a look again at the table from section one, which shows how a score is awarded.</p>
<p>A normal baby has an APGAR score of ten at one minute and ten at five minutes. A score between seven and ten is considered to be normal. Approximately 70% of newborns score seven or better.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Sign</th><th>Score 0</th><th>Score 1</th><th>Score 2</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Appearance</td><td>Blue, pale</td><td>Body pink, extremities bluish</td><td>Pink all over</td></tr><tr><td>Pulse/heart rate</td><td>Absent</td><td>&lt; 100/min</td><td>&gt; 100/min</td></tr><tr><td>Grimace</td><td>None</td><td>Grimace</td><td>Cry</td></tr><tr><td>Activity</td><td>Limb</td><td>Some flexion</td><td>Spontaneous movements</td></tr><tr><td>Respiration</td><td>Absent</td><td>Hypoventilation/gasping</td><td>Vigorous crying</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A score at five minutes gives a more accurate prediction regarding survival. A low score at five minutes is, therefore, more serious than a low score at one minute after birth. Notify paediatrician if score is six or below at five minutes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="subsequent-care">Subsequent Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subsequent-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You need to be familiar with the daily management of a neonate and what nursing activities are undertaken.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 120 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Try to list the principles of daily care of a neonate.</p>
<p>The principles of management of the neonate include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintenance of the established respiration</li>
<li>Provision of nutrition</li>
<li>Prevention from infection</li>
<li>Provision of warmth</li>
<li>Protection from injury</li>
<li>Assessment of the progress of the baby</li>
<li>Education of the mother as to the further care and management of the baby</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now go through these principles in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance-of-the-established-respiration">Maintenance of the Established Respiration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-the-established-respiration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A normal baby should continue to breathe and maintain a good skin colour without medical intervention.</p>
<p>A baby who tends to produce a lot of mucus should be closely watched and the airway cleared frequently, because this may tend to interfere with breathing by blocking the airway. The head of the cot should also be lowered in such circumstances. Measures should be taken to avoid suffocation from the pillow, clothes covering the baby or mother lying over the baby.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="provision-of-nutrition">Provision of Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#provision-of-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Breast feeding is an accepted and ideal means of providing nutrition to a neonate. The neonate should be put on the breast immediately, as long as their condition allows this. Demand feeding (baby led breast feeding) is ideal and should be advocated. Encourage the mother to breast feed exclusively in order to avoid the need for the addition of other fluids. The mother's milk has adequate water to meet the needs of the infant. Therefore, there is no need to give the baby additional fluids (contrary to the belief of some mothers that babies require water).</p>
<p>To ensure that the baby gets both fore and hind milk, the mother needs to breast feed the baby on one breast until completely empty. This ensures that the baby has all the nutrients, because foremilk contains proteins and hind milk is high in calories. Bring up wind before offering the second breast to the baby. If the baby is not able to suckle the second one until it is completely empty, then the mother is advised to express milk, in order for fresh milk to be released to the breast. The nipples should be cared for to avoid complications such as sore nipples that will affect the baby's breast feeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="provision-of-warmth">Provision of Warmth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#provision-of-warmth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The baby should be kept at a comfortable temperature. Care should be taken not to overheat the baby, as is sometimes the habit of mothers.</p>
<p>Mothers in the tropics, for instance, often tend to overdress the neonates. Mothers should be taught about appropriate clothing for varied climates. They should dress the baby according to the change of environmental temperature.</p>
<p>Baby wraps should be loose enough to allow for free movement of the legs and arms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protection-from-injury-and-infection">Protection from Injury and Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protection-from-injury-and-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Injuries may be inflicted by the long nails of the mother, midwife, the baby itself, or sharp instruments, for example, the safety pin used to secure nappies. Injuries from falls, scalding and burns are not unusual.</p>
<p>The midwife should instruct the mother on how to handle her baby, and teach her how to wrap napkins without using safety pins. She should also be instructed to keep her nails short.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-from-infection">Prevention from Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-from-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infection, especially cross infection, can be minimised by encouraging mothers to handle their own babies. Anybody in contact with the child should be encouraged to wash their hands before handling the baby.</p>
<p>Visitors should be controlled, especially in a lying in ward.</p>
<p>This helps control infection. Midwives or other attendants with a cold or infections foci, should not work with babies. Babies born at home should be nursed indoors, away from visitors for the first eight days.</p>
<p>Immunisation should be administered to protect the neonate from certain preventable diseases. BCG and oral polio should be given within the first 24hrs after delivery. One of the advantages of breast feeding is that it protects the baby against childhood diseases since the breast milk is rich in immunoglobulins.</p>
<p>The cord is one of the sources of entry for microorganisms in an infant. The aim of cord care is to prevent haemorrhage, while getting the cord to dry up and separate. To this end, you should check on the cord hourly, because bleeding may occur if the ligature slips off or as the Wharton's</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>jelly shrinks. This is why a thick cord is more likely to bleed. If there is bleeding, then it should be legated.</p>
<p>The cord should then be observed more closely.</p>
<p>The cord is best left exposed and mothers should be advised not to use any remedies on the cord since it predisposes to infection.</p>
<p>The midwife should discourage mothers from touching the cord.</p>
<p>When the dry cord breaks off, it may leave a raw area. This should be cleaned with spirit and dressed with 1% Gentian violet. Use spirit because it leaves the site dry. Other antiseptics leave the place damp, making it ideal for the multiplication of micro-organisms.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>If the cord fails to drop off by the sixth day, it may mean that there is an infection.</p>
<p><strong>Skin Care</strong></p>
<p>The neonate's skin is fragile and easily bruised. Therefore, irritants such as antiseptics, fabric softeners and starch are discouraged.</p>
<p>Creased hard fabrics, stool and urine may interfere with the skin integrity. To prevent damage to the baby's skin, liquid paraffin preparations may be used because they serve as good cleansers.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>You should report any abnormalities observed on the umbilical stump such as redness, unpleasant odour or bleeding because these are signs of infection.</p>
<p><strong>Assessment of Baby's Growth</strong></p>
<p>The midwife should be able to determine that the baby is healthy and thriving. A baby who is healthy and is growing is active, feeds well, is free from infection and gains weight steadily. In order to observe these, it is necessary to examine the baby thoroughly at least once a day during bath time.</p>
<p>The following daily observations should be recorded in order to determine the baby's health status:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>General appearance and activity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Exclude any discharge from the eyes and ears which may be an indicator of infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The skin should be checked to detect the presence of jaundice, pallor or cyanosis, septic spots or sore buttocks</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check the mouth to exclude oral thrush</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The umbilical cord should be examined to ensure that it is drying up and is not septic</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weigh the baby to determine weight gain</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Other general care measures include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Observations, especially on respiration</li>
<li>Feeding patterns</li>
<li>Crying</li>
<li>Urinary output</li>
<li>Character of stool</li>
</ul>
<p>Depending on what is observed, document and report to the doctor if necessary. In this way, abnormalities will be detected and corrective measures taken early enough.</p>
<p><strong>Education of the Mother</strong></p>
<p>This should start during the antenatal period. Emphasis should be laid on the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Personal hygiene and general cleanliness</li>
<li>How to care for the baby (especially for the primigravidae)</li>
<li>Exclusive breast feeding</li>
<li>Attendance of post-natal clinic, family planning and infant welfare clinics</li>
</ul>
<p>You have now come to the end of the subsection on the normal neonate and how to manage them. This started with immediate care then subsequent care. The health or well being of the neonate depends on how the environment has been modified for its survival.</p>
<p>In the next subsection you will focus on high risk neonates. Some of the conditions you are going to cover include circumstances you may meet in the labour ward, post-natal ward or newborn unit. The neonate may not be sick but it may be at a potential high risk both physically, psychologically and socially.</p>
<p><strong>The High Risk Neonate</strong></p>
<p>In this subsection, you will begin looking at neonates at risk. You will then move on to neonates found in abnormal circumstances, for example, babies born before their due date and those who are abandoned.</p>
<p>Usually, maternal conditions may predispose a neonate to be at high risk of developing the disorders you are about to cover. The high risk groups of neonates require early diagnosis so that the disorders can either be prevented or appropriate measures instituted early enough.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-high-risk-neonates">Classification of High Risk Neonates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-high-risk-neonates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Try to list at least five types of high risk neonates due to maternal conditions.</p>
<p>You should have included the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Low birth weight (this category includes babies weighing less than 2500gm regardless of the estimated period of gestation)</li>
<li>Post term babies</li>
<li>Diabetic infant</li>
<li>Rh negative mother (see Jaundice)</li>
<li>HIV/AIDS positive mother</li>
<li>VDRL positive mother</li>
<li>Hepatitis positive mother</li>
<li>Neonatal sepsis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-premature-infant-preterm">The Premature Infant (Preterm)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-premature-infant-preterm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A preterm infant is a baby born before the 37th completed week of gestation.</p>
<p>A high percentage of premature births occur with female births and pregnancies with multiple foetuses. This is most often due to the early over distension of the uterus, which leads to the foetus being born prematurely. Premature births also occur more frequently in low socio economic and illiterate groups in the population, largely as a result of the poor nutritional intake of the pregnant mother. Additionally, they tend to be more common when there is concurrent maternal metabolic or systemic disease, for example, hypertension and renal disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="try-to-list-two-causes-of-prematurity">Try to list two causes of prematurity.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#try-to-list-two-causes-of-prematurity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You should note that in many instances the cause of premature birth is not known. However, some of the causal factors are thought to be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Multiple births (twins or more), which causes early distension of the uterus hence early birth</li>
<li>Hypertension associated with the pregnancy leading to early induction of labour, for example, preeclampsia and eclampsia</li>
<li>Premature rupture of membranes due to physical or psychological stress</li>
</ul>
<p>Prematurity is also associated with:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Polyhydramnios which causes over distension</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Trauma leading to premature rupture of membranes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chronic infections or diseases in the mother, such as syphilis, tuberculosis, chronic nephritis, cardiac disease, diabetes and thyroid disease, may lead to premature labour</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acute infections in the mother, like pneumonia, influenza, rheumatic fever and malaria could induce premature labour</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical stress caused by non obstetric surgery may lead to premature labour if the mother has this procedure while pregnant</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Congenital malformation of the foetus</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Habitual abortion owing to incompetent cervical OS or uterine malformation</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>You should remember that premature labour can be prevented.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-of-premature-birth">Prevention of Premature Birth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-premature-birth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are a number of things you can do to prevent a premature birth. Can you remember them? Try to recall what you covered in unit two.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="state-two-ways-you-can-prevent-premature-births">State two ways you can prevent premature births.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#state-two-ways-you-can-prevent-premature-births" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>One way to prevent premature births is to give early and continued prenatal care with stress on dietary and general hygienic education to the expectant mother. This will also ensure immediate treatment of those complications of pregnancy likely to cause, or be associated with, premature labour.</p>
<p>Sometimes it is also possible to postpone or inhibit uterine contractions in some cases of premature labour through the use of certain pharmaceutical agents such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Those that act by preventing the release or synthesis of a known uterine stimulant, for example, prostaglandin inhibitors, non steroidal anti inflammatory drugs like aspirin, endomethacin, declofenac</li>
<li>Those that act by the direct effect on the myometrial cells, for example, beta adrenergic receptor stimulants like retodrine, fenoterol, salbutamol</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember that inhibition of preterm labour is contra indicated in the case of certain conditions, where inhibition may compromise the life of the pregnant woman. These conditions include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Eclampsia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe preeclampsia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antepartum haemorrhage, especially abruptio placentae</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chronic renal disease</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe chronic hypertension</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advanced cardiac disease</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foetal distress</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chorioamnionitis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foetal death</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foetal growth retardation</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember:
Inhibition of preterm labour should not be considered routine in all cases of suspected premature labour because it may be detrimental to the mother's or infant's survival.</p>
<p>Other ways to prevent premature birth include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prolonged bed rest should be encouraged, especially where the mother has any of the conditions that predispose to preterm labour</li>
<li>Use of sedatives during preterm labour to ensure complete bed rest</li>
<li>Avoidance of strenuous exercise and calming the mother, because any strain or stress may aggravate preterm labour</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember that there is still a lot more research to be done on causation of premature labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical-characteristics-of-prematurity">Physical Characteristics of Prematurity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-characteristics-of-prematurity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Generally the characteristics depend on the gestational age. The generalised description is that the baby may appear pink or dark red, hands and feet may be cyanosed and may be jaundiced early.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wakefulness">Wakefulness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wakefulness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the infant is awake, the lower extremities are rarely extended. There may be slow prolonged contraction of the facial muscles, quivering movements or transient smiles. There may also be fine movements of the fingers and toes. These may be confused with convulsions but they are not.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cry">Cry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cry is feebler than that of a full term infant. In fact, a premature infant usually cries very little, if at all.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skin-and-appendages">Skin and Appendages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skin-and-appendages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The skin is covered by a small amount of vernix caseosa. Lanugo is present on the sides of the face and on the extremities and the back. There is scanty hair on the head and the eyebrows are</p>
<p>usually absent. The nipples and areola are inconspicuous. The nails are soft.</p>
<p>Generalised oedema is apparent at birth and later the tissue fluid decreases, leaving the skin loose and wrinkled. Blood vessels can be easily seen under the skin because subcutaneous tissue is thin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neck-and-thorax">Neck and Thorax<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neck-and-thorax" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The thorax is cone shaped and the rib cage is weak, owing to immature osseous calcification. Obstruction to the free flow of air causes marked sternal retraction, a rapid heart rate and respiratory noises. Occasionally, cardiac murmurs are heard. A change in position may cause periods of apnoea. Very small infants will not open the mouth to breathe. The nose should therefore be checked for occlusion frequently.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="favourable-prognostic-signs">Favourable Prognostic Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#favourable-prognostic-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The premature neonate has a higher chance of survival if:</p>
<ul>
<li>Birth weight is more than 1500g</li>
<li>There is no persistent cyanosis and there is some activity on stimulation</li>
<li>Gagging and swallowing reflexes are fairly active</li>
<li>Skin is not wrinkled and subcutaneous fat is present</li>
<li>Body temperature is stable</li>
<li>There are no signs of abnormal conditions such as jaundice, pallor and/or sternal retraction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-a-premature-baby">Management of a Premature Baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-a-premature-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management-of-a-premature-infant">Management of a premature infant<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-a-premature-infant" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Avoid depression of the foetal respiratory centre</li>
<li>Sedatives of opium derivatives should not be used during premature labour</li>
<li>Shorten the perineal phase during delivery of a preterm baby by performing an episiotomy. As this will reduce the possibility of intracranial injury</li>
<li>Transfer a woman in premature labour to a well equipped hospital for adequate resuscitation and care of the premature infant</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 125 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-of-a-premature-infant">Care of a premature infant<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-a-premature-infant" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The efficient care of the premature infant is equally important. You should take the following steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Clear the airway using a fine mucus extractor/catheter</li>
<li>Administer oxygen at 1 litre per minute till respiration is well established and colour is satisfactory</li>
<li>Put the infant in an incubator or cover with warm towels and transfer to a special baby care unit as soon as practicable</li>
<li>Ideally infants weighing less than 2 kilograms that have been delivered in a health centre or in the home should be transferred to a well equipped hospital with nursery for baby care</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incubators may be lacking in some the health facilities. The midwife must, therefore, learn to improvise on how to keep the baby warm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="further-management-aims-of-a-premature-infant">Further management aims of a premature infant<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#further-management-aims-of-a-premature-infant" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once immediate steps have been taken to ensure the well being of the premature infant, further management aims at:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintenance of respiration and good colour</li>
<li>Provision of warmth</li>
<li>Prevention of infection</li>
<li>Ensuring good progress and growth</li>
<li>Educating the mother to take care of her infant</li>
<li>Ensuring baby gets adequate nutrition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance-of-respiration-of-the-preterm-baby">Maintenance of Respiration of the Preterm Baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-respiration-of-the-preterm-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should assist in the establishment of respiration since the respiratory centre in the medulla is immature. The lungs tend to be atelectatic and are not well developed due to inadequate surfactant. The diaphragm and chest muscles are weak, therefore, the baby is constantly asphyxiated. This means that the airway should be repeatedly cleared. The infant should be laid with its head to one side and the foot of the cot should be slightly raised to aid with the drainage of mucus. You should also watch the infant closely for signs of respiratory distress and cyanosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Respiratory distress can be recognised by the rapid, irregular respiration with periods of apnoea, in-drawing of the chest walls and sternal recession and expiratory grunt with cyanosis of body and face.</p>
<p>Give oxygen in such cases (avoid high concentrations of oxygen) to the premature infant. The recommended dosage is 30 - 40%. Note that prolonged administration of a high concentration of oxygen may lead to the development of fibrous tissue behind the lens, which results in a condition known as retrolental fibroplasia leading to blindness in the newborn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="provision-of-warmth-and-maintenance-of-body-temperature">Provision of Warmth and Maintenance of Body Temperature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#provision-of-warmth-and-maintenance-of-body-temperature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The midwife should do her best to ensure that the baby's temperature is prevented from reaching very low levels. Remember that the heat regulation centre in premature babies is underdeveloped. Small babies weighing less than 1.5 kilograms should ideally be nursed in an incubator with temperature of about 30 degrees Celsius and relative humidity of 65%. If there is no incubator available, they should be nursed in warm towels (which may be warmed with hot water bottles). You can also make an improvised cot out of a wooden box raised off the floor where there are no cots.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Use of cotton wool as a means of keeping infant warm has been condemned, since it deprives the skin of air and there is danger of infection and overheating of infant.</p>
<p>Loose flannel clothing is recommended for infants nursed in cots (woollen material may cause a skin rash and is also cumbersome). The infant should not be exposed to direct sunlight. If the premature infant can maintain its body temperature at 36 degrees Celsius, its condition is likely to improve and it may be weaned off the incubator.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="feeding">Feeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#feeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Breast milk is ideal because of its digestibility, nutrients and the immunity it gives to the newborn. The practice of withholding feeds or fluid for 24 hours or more before feeding is considered unnecessary.</p>
<p>If the stomach content is aspirated before the first feed, regurgitation and inhalation of</p>
<p>stomach contents are not likely. The first feed should be small and ideally given per tube. Five percent glucose water may be given, which has the advantage of counteracting acidosis and provides fluid and energy.</p>
<p>If the infant can tolerate it expressed breast milk should be offered next. The amount of feeds given depends on the size of the infant and its tolerance levels. However, 10mls is usually offered for the first few feeds. Infection control and prevention measures are highly recommended with regard to handling expressed milk.</p>
<p>Artificial milk, that is half strength cow's milk, lactogen and so on, may be resorted to only if the mother is in poor condition. The recommended amount is 90mls of milk per kilogram of body weight per day for the first week of life. This is followed by 150mls for the second week and 180 - 210mls per kilogram of body weight during the third week. To avoid over distension of the stomach, vomiting and subsequent inhalation, small feeds, of greater concentration, are given at one to two hourly intervals.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Try always to treat each infant individually and give the amount of milk the individual infant needs, depending on their appetite, tolerance to feeds and general condition.</p>
<p><strong>Method of feeding</strong></p>
<p>The method of feeding is determined by the infant's size, general health and presence of sucking and swallowing reflexes.</p>
<p>Breast feed as soon as the infant's condition allows. Infants of 1.8 kilograms and over, with good sucking and swallowing reflexes, may be spoon fed. In cases where neither of the aforementioned options is possible, naso-gastric tube feeding is preferred because once instituted it can be left for a week before it is changed and carries less risk of bronchial aspiration. The latter is often associated with oro-gastric feeding, especially if the tube is not well pinched when being withdrawn.</p>
<p><strong>Naso-gastric method of feeding</strong></p>
<p>Should you decide to use the naso-gastric method of tube feeding the following points should be taken into consideration:</p>
<ul>
<li>A small size polythene tube (polytex) should be used for feeding infants weighing 1500g or less. A rubber catheter FG10 can also be used.</li>
<li>Although the tubes come in pre-sterilised packets, it is advisable to boil them for a few minutes before use to make them supple and easy to pass.</li>
<li>The arms of the infant are wrapped and the head of the cot raised.</li>
<li>The nostrils should be cleared with wet cotton swabs.</li>
<li>The required length of the tube to be passed is determined by measuring from the bridge of the infant's nose to its sternum. It should be marked before boiling (polytex tubes are already marked).</li>
<li>When the tube is passed, the stomach contents are aspirated and tested with blue litmus paper. Red discolouration means the tube is in the stomach.</li>
<li>The aspirate colour and amount should be noted and recorded.</li>
</ul>
<p>â˜ If the aspirate consists of clear milk it should be returned and the feed decreased by same amount.
â˜ If the aspirate is blood or bile stained discard and replace by equal volume of normal saline in the intravenous fluids.
â˜ The barrel of a syringe is used as a funnel for giving the feeds which should be allowed to flow by gravity and not pushed by a syringe piston.
â˜ The amount of feed the infant has taken is recorded.
â˜ After feeding, the baby is left to rest quietly on their back with the head turned to one side or made to lie on the right side for 15 minutes.</p>
<p><strong>General Feeding Steps to be Taken</strong></p>
<p>The following steps should generally be taken when feeding the baby:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cleanliness must be observed. Feeding utensils should be decontaminated and soaked in a solution of jik (1:6) for 10 minutes then dried.</li>
<li>Wind should be brought up by raising the infant to sitting position or gently rolling them against your hand or rubbing their back with your right hand. Naso-gastric feeding infants do not require this.</li>
<li>The baby should be put on the right side after feeding with the head of the cot raised to allow any vomited milk to run out of the mouth.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>You should always have an aspirator at hand to remove regurgitated milk from the naso-pharynx.</li>
<li>Record the actual amount of feed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Supplements of vitamins A, B, C, D, folic acid and iron are usually given to the premature infant because they have no store of iron, vitamins and mineral salts before birth. Artificial feeds cannot provide all the nutritional needs of an infant.</p>
<ul>
<li>Staff in baby care unit should be in good health and have no foci of infection or colds.</li>
<li>Staff should be meticulous in cleanliness and should be proficient at resuscitation of the baby.</li>
<li>Frequent hand washing is imperative in a premature baby nursery. Principles of infection prevention should always be practiced (see module one).</li>
<li>Visitors should not be allowed into the premature unit because they may bring in micro-organisms.</li>
<li>Only the parents should handle the infant if nursed at home or maternity centre.</li>
<li>The infant should not be brought out into the open until it can maintain its body temperature.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-infection">Prevention of Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Preterm infants are very susceptible to infection, therefore:</p>
<ul>
<li>In hospital, the parents are only allowed to view their babies through the glass windows of the incubator. The mother should be taught how to handle the baby because her touch is important for development of the mother/baby relationship.</li>
<li>The nursery must be kept clean. Damp dusting or mopping is preferred to sweeping and dry dusting to minimise spread of micro-organisms.</li>
<li>Avoid direct draughts in the nursery by keeping the windows shut.</li>
<li>Infants in lying-in wards or maternity centres must sleep under a net. Infectious babies should be isolated and potentially infected babies should be given prophylactic antibiotics.</li>
<li>The incubator should be cleaned every day and the water changed and disinfected because an incubator provides an ideal environment for organisms to multiply.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="try-to-write-down-at-least-four-observations-you-need-to-make-to-monitor-the-progress-of-the-premature-infant">Try to write down at least four observations you need to make to monitor the progress of the premature infant.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#try-to-write-down-at-least-four-observations-you-need-to-make-to-monitor-the-progress-of-the-premature-infant" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Respiration of the infant, that is, do they exhibit laboured breathing and periods of apnoea. The respiration rate should be taken and recorded four hourly or more frequently, in case it is unsatisfactory.</li>
<li>The temperature should also be recorded four hourly since fever and hypothermia are bad signs. A premature neonate who is progressing should be able to maintain their body temperature.</li>
<li>Auscultation of the heart and recording of the heart rate (Apex beat).</li>
<li>Observe closely for colour changes like jaundice occurring within 24 - 36 hours of birth. This is a serious occurrence, which must be reported. Other colour changes include cyanosis, pallor and greyness are also significant and should also be reported.</li>
<li>Rashes, discharge from the eyes or moist umbilical cord, grey colour and constantly low temperature are usually signs of infection and should also be reported.</li>
<li>Note the amount of feed taken by the infant, the method of feeding and any vomiting of feeds.</li>
<li>Abdominal distension and oedema of the face, abdomen and legs should be reported if severe.</li>
<li>Note if the infant is passing urine well. Absence of urine in the first 24 hours must be reported. Frequent stools also are noted. Loose stools may indicate infection.</li>
<li>The neonate should be weighed 12 - 24 hours after birth. Thereafter, weighing is usually done twice weekly because weight gain is usually slow. Weight loss in a premature infant should not alarm the midwife, provided the infant's general condition is satisfactory and there is no vomiting.</li>
<li>The haemoglobin level should be estimated at birth and thereafter on a weekly basis to exclude anaemia.</li>
<li>The general behaviour of the infant with</li>
</ol>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>particular attention to its activity should be noted.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="response-to-noise">Response to Noise<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#response-to-noise" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A premature infant responds to noise in a similar way to a mature baby. There is evidence that excessive noise is detrimental to the development of normal hearing and can be stress provoking for the sick baby.</p>
<p>The midwife should, therefore, be aware of these possible deleterious effects and take steps to reduce noise levels where possible. During periods of quietness, it is customary to dim lights. Longer quiet sleep patterns are related to better weight gain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="education-of-the-mother">Education of the Mother<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#education-of-the-mother" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Time and patience are necessary to reorientate the mother, whether she is a primipara or multipara. The mother may see the infant as a fragile little being and is often scared of handling them. It is necessary to introduce the mother gradually to handling, feeding and general care under supervision before discharge. In some hospitals, the mothers stay in a mother's home and come up to the premature unit every three hours to feed and nurse their infants under supervision.</p>
<p>Mothers should be allowed to look after infants whose weights are 1.8 kilograms and over. Breast feeding should be encouraged and if the baby is on artificial feeds for any reason, the midwife should ensure that the mother is able to prepare the feeds.</p>
<p>When the baby is ready for discharge, an arrangement should be made for the mother to room in for two to three days to enable her to undertake the 24 hour responsibility of care. It is advisable to discharge the infant when they are 2kg or over, have a constant temperature and are able to feed well.</p>
<p>You should educate the mother on feeding, winding and bathing the baby and how to avoid gastroenteritis and respiratory infections. Immunisation should be given when the child attains a weight of 2 kilograms and should be followed up in a paediatric special clinic until the developmental milestone is passed. The mother should also be encouraged to attend follow up sessions in a child welfare clinic until her child is five years old.</p>
<p>As a health worker, you should be aware, and you should make the mother aware, of the fact that a premature baby is prone to the following complications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cyanotic attacks</li>
<li>Cerebral haemorrhage</li>
<li>Heart failure and pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>Jaundice</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Poor mental and intellectual development in later years</li>
<li>Respiratory Distress Syndrome</li>
</ul>
<p>The baby's care giver, both in and out of the hospital environment, should maintain constant vigilance for any symptoms of the aforementioned conditions.</p>
<p>Next you will look at the other type of low birth weight infant.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-small-for-gestational-age-infant">The Small for Gestational Age Infant<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-small-for-gestational-age-infant" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The small for gestational age (SGA) infant may be a full term infant who appears small for their age. The clinical appearance of this infant may be of several types. The first type is:</p>
<ul>
<li>Low weight for gestational age</li>
